Without it she would have to face the question of who she is in the absence of a future to prevent — a question the file suggests she has not yet fully answered. The mission is genuine and morally serious, but it also **defends against the developmental task of post-trauma identity-construction without external referent.**

#### 7.5.3 Costume and Codename Progression
Hound → Phoenix → Marvel Girl → Mother Askani → Prestige. Each rename is a **re-self-authorship**, an attempt to claim a new compensatory identity over the old wound. The progression is meaningful: each name is more her own than the last. "Prestige" — the magician's term for the third act of the trick, the return — is the most self-aware codename in the X-canon and announces the recovery project explicitly.

#### 7.5.4 Religion (Askani) as Externalized Containment
The Askani sisterhood is not metaphor — she actually built it. Functionally it served as **externalized superego and externalized hope**: a structure outside herself that could hold meaning when her own capacity faltered. Most trauma survivors at best join such structures; she founded one. This compensatory move ranks among the most ambitious in the entire X-corpus.

---

### 7.6 Negative Compensations / Costs

For completeness, the file must record the defenses that **cost more than they pay**:

- **Hyper-competence as concealment**: she performs operational excellence partly to forestall inquiry into her inner state. Teammates underestimate her distress because her output stays high.
- **Surveillance-orientation as relating**: she gathers psi-data on people she loves, often without explicit consent, because intimacy-through-information is the only intimacy the Hound era taught her. She has worked on this, but it recurs under stress.
- **Anticipatory grief preempting present joy**: she struggles to enjoy a present she has already mourned. Korvus and the late-era Jean reunion both surface this cost.
- **Mission-purity as relational refusal**: when forced to choose between the mission and a relationship, she chooses the mission with a speed that disturbs the partner. The choice is correct often enough that she has not been forced to revisit it, but it has cost her bonds.
- **Identification-with-aggressor residue**: she retains tactical comfort with methods (deep psi-invasion, predatory tracking) that the rest of the team finds ethically difficult. She has rules about when she will use them; the rules are hers, not the team's, and this has produced friction.

---

### 7.7 Summary Ranking

From most primitive to most mature, with current load-bearing weight in parentheses (decade-late assessment):

1. Somatic telekinetic discharge *(low, declining)*
2. Phoenix-bonded delusional projection *(state-dependent, episodic)*
3. Dissociative temporal flight *(low, held in reserve)*
4. Splitting (Phoenix-axis) *(moderate)*
5. Identification with the aggressor *(high, partially integrated)*
6. Projective identification *(moderate)*
7. Acting out *(low, declining)*
8. Passive aggression (Scott-axis) *(low, largely resolved)*
9. Regression under restraint *(moderate, trigger-bound)*
10. Reaction formation (child-protection) *(high, partially matured)*
11. Intellectualization via temporal framing *(high, signature)*
12. Isolation of affect *(moderate, content-specific)*
13. Undoing (Askani) *(historically high, now identity-integrated)*
14. Displacement *(moderate, semi-conscious)*
15. Reparative identification (Jean, Storm) *(high, adaptive)*
16. Sublimation *(high, increasing)*
17. Altruism *(high, mature)*
18. Anticipation *(very high, double-edged)*
19. Humor *(emerging, prognostically excellent)*
20. Suppression *(emerging)*

The architecture is **bottom-heavy but top-growing.** She still has the full primitive stack available and uses it under sufficient pressure; she has also, against considerable structural odds, developed a functioning mature layer. Few subjects in the corpus show this much *vertical range* in their defensive repertoire, and fewer still show it with this much self-awareness about which layer they are operating from at any given moment. That self-awareness is, at the file's close, the most prognostically encouraging finding: she watches her own defenses operate, names them, and — increasingly — chooses among them.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: RACHEL ANNE SUMMERS

## Subsection 6 of File — Decade-by-Decade Clinical Mapping

A note on chronology before we begin. Rachel's lived time and her published time do not align, and her subjective age does not align with either. The decades below are organized by **publication-era cohort**, because that is how the behavioral evidence is stratified, but each section reckons internally with her concurrent subjective state — Hound adolescence, displaced young adulthood, Askani middle age, resurrected post-Krakoan integration. The clinician reading this file should understand that Rachel is, at any given moment, processing trauma at multiple temporal indices simultaneously. That is itself a diagnostic feature, not a framing artifact.

---

### Era I: 1981–1984 — The Pre-History (Hound Adolescence, observed retroactively)

We have no contemporaneous behavior from this era; what we have is the silhouette of it, derived from her own later flashbacks (*UXM* #189, #199; *Excalibur* dream sequences; the Askani recollections in *Adventures of Cyclops & Phoenix* #2) and from her behavioral baseline on arrival in 1985, which is the residue of this period.

**Affect regulation in the Hound years** was almost certainly produced through engineered dissociation. The Ahab program required a captive child telepath to track and collar her own kind; this is not survivable with affect intact. The conditioning split her into an operational self (cold, scanning, predatory, obedient) and a witnessing self (horrified, dormant, walled off). When the operational self acted, the witnessing self was anesthetized — by inhibitor collar, by psi-suppression, by the simple repetition that makes atrocity routine. This is the structural origin of the splitting documented in Section 3. Per van der Kolk's model of structural dissociation (Apparently Normal Part / Emotional Part), the Hound *was* the ANP — the functional, action-capable surface — and the witnessing child was the EP, held in suspension behind it.

**Cognitive style in this era** was almost certainly hypervigilant-tactical: tracking, pattern-matching, threat-anticipation, all without narrative integration. She knew what she was doing; she did not allow herself to know that she knew.

**Self-concept was effectively annihilated.** "Hound #N2-3175" is a designation, not an identity. The recovery of "Rachel" as a name and a self begins only at the moment of treason — the psi-link with Kate, *UXM* #141 — and that recovery is not complete for decades.

---

### Era II: 1985–1988 — Arrival and Disintegration (Claremont's Core Run)

This is the period in which Rachel becomes clinically legible. The behavioral record here is dense and consistent.

**Affect regulation: severely impaired, cycling rapid.** The typical Rachel-scene in 1985–1986 contains, within a single page-turn, four distinct affective states: hypervigilant scan → recognition-flash → grief surge → either rage discharge or freeze collapse. The cycling is too fast to be modulated. Issues #184 (arrival), #189 (the dream-issue, where she revisits the camps in sleep and the mansion's defenses register a Sentinel-level threat in her bedroom), #199 (the Holocaust Memorial), and #207 (Selene) all document this pattern. She does not have access to titration; she is either numb or flooded. The window of tolerance, in Ogden's sense, is vanishingly narrow.

**Cognitive style: hypervigilant-narrativizing, with paranoid features.** She is constantly reading futures — she perceives the present as a thin film over a known catastrophic outcome. This makes her tactically brilliant in short timescales (she clocks rooms, identifies threats, predicts moves) and catastrophically bad at sustained planning, because every plan is contaminated by the camps-future. The intellectualization-via-temporal-framing noted in Section 3 begins here: she translates immediate distress into strategic urgency, which both grants meaning and forecloses grieving.

**Self-concept: fragmented, conditional, predator-shadowed.** She does not believe she has the right to the Summers name. The famous nursery scene with infant Nathan (*UXM* #201) is diagnostically rich — she is holding the brother who, in her timeline, was never born, and weeping over an absence she cannot articulate. She does not believe Scott will claim her; she does not test the hypothesis; she watches from rooftops. This is not paranoid delusion. It is the realistic projection of a child whose every adult attachment in formative years was either murdered or actively predatory. Bowlby would call this an internal working model corrupted at the root.

**Defenses in this era are primitive and load-bearing.** Splitting is the dominant operation. Phoenix, when she claims it at the Memorial, is immediately a both-good-and-bad object she cannot hold in unity. Identification with the aggressor remains active — when she hunts Selene, the technique is the Hound's, and she knows it, and she does it anyway. Reaction formation organizes her protective stance toward children. There is, as yet, almost no capacity for mentalization in Fonagy's sense — she cannot reliably hold another person's mind in her own without distortion, which is why she keeps misreading what Scott, Storm, and Kate are actually offering her.

The era closes with two near-death assaults (Selene's blade, Sabretooth's mauling) and a hand-off into Excalibur, where the affective intensity drops because the surrounding cast is constitutionally less wounded than the X-Men proper. This is the first stabilization.

---

### Era III: 1988–1993 — Excalibur and the Lateral Family (Subacute Recovery)

Excalibur is, in clinical terms, a therapeutic milieu. The British team — Kurt, Kitty, Meggan, Brian — operates at a lower trauma baseline than the X-Men, and Rachel's affect regulation visibly improves under this ambient calm.

**Affect regulation: improving, episodic.** The rapid cycling persists but the periods between flares lengthen. She develops, for the first time, the capacity for non-mission interaction — meals, banter, sustained physical proximity to others without scanning. The presence of Kurt is particularly stabilizing; he is one of the few characters in the canon who can touch her without warning and not trigger a defensive flare, because his own affect is so reliably warm that her body learns him as safe. This is corrective relational experience in the precise sense Alexander used the term.

**Cognitive style: still pattern-seeking and future-oriented, but with the first signs of present-tense engagement.** She begins to make choices that have no instrumental relation to the camps-prevention drive. She trains with Kitty for the sake of training. She mourns Captain Britain's deaths and resurrections without immediately translating them into strategic re-evaluations. This is genuine cognitive expansion.

**Self-concept: still negative-valenced, but with a tentative role-identity ("Phoenix, member of Excalibur") that is not solely defined by atonement.** The Phoenix-bonding stabilizes in this period — she holds it without the *UXM* #207 immolation-threats — and this is significant. The cosmic force has, briefly, become an instrument rather than an identity. She is not Phoenix; she has Phoenix. This is the first integration.

The period ends with the Siege Perilous / timestream rebound that catapults her two thousand years forward. The progress made here will not be lost — but it will be subjected to a stress test of cosmic proportion.

---

### Era IV: 1994–1996 (subjective: decades) — The Askani Period (Mother Askani)

This is the most clinically remarkable phase in the entire record, and it is dramatically underrepresented in screen-time relative to its psychological weight. From Rachel's interior perspective, this era lasts decades. She arrives in the post-apocalyptic far future as a stranded young woman and lives to old age there. The published material (*Adventures of Cyclops & Phoenix*, *Askani'son*, scattered *Cable* backmatter) shows us a woman who has done the impossible: built a sustained, generative, externally-oriented life out of the wreckage of her trauma.

**Affect regulation: substantially improved through ritual containment.** The Askani order is, functionally, a trauma-informed religious practice she designed for herself. The chants, the meditations, the codified language ("the dreamtime," "this one"), the third-person self-reference she adopts as Mother Askani — these are containers. The third-person self-reference is especially telling: it is the same technique Pennebaker and Kross have shown produces affective distance and improved regulation in highly distressed subjects. She *engineered her own intervention*. She also, in the same period, accelerates her own somatic decay by channeling the Phoenix-force to keep the order's mission alive — meaning her improved regulation runs concurrent with a terminal-illness awareness she does not flinch from. This is acceptance in the Eriksonian late-stage sense, achieved decades before chronological warrant.

**Cognitive style: shifts from tactical-anticipatory to strategic-generational.** The branching probability trees remain her native medium, but the time horizon expands from the next combat round to the next millennium. She is playing for the salvation of Nathan/Cable across a two-thousand-year arc. This requires — and she develops — a capacity for delayed gratification and sustained hope under conditions of total isolation that her younger self could not have approximated. The catastrophizing recedes because she is now living *inside* the catastrophe and finds it survivable.

**Self-concept: transformed via role-occupation.** "Mother Askani" is not a costume; it is a real identity she lives into and that lives into her. She becomes the calm-authority maternal figure she once needed and never had — and there is a deep psychological logic to this: the only way she can finally receive that mothering is to *embody* it for someone else. Cable is, in this sense, her therapeutic object as well as her charge. Her self-concept stabilizes around competence, generativity, and faith — three pillars that her earlier self had no access to.

**The dying.** She dies in this era, old and depleted. The Phoenix-channeling and the timestream burden consume her. Crucially, the record shows her dying *integrated*. There is no Phoenix-flare, no temporal flight, no Hound regression. She dies as Mother Askani, in her order, with her work substantially complete. From a developmental standpoint this is closure — a death she chose, in service of a future she built. The fact that she will subsequently be recovered from the timestream and resume her life does not retroactively erase the integration achieved here. The Askani-self is now a permanent stratum of her psyche.

---

### Era V: 1998–2010 — The Return and the Plateau (Marvel Girl, X-Treme X-Men, Legacy)

She comes back young, or apparently young — her chronological age is now a metaphysical question — and she comes back as Marvel Girl, junior team member, surrounded by people who do not know what she has been. The Askani integration is present but covert; she does not lead with it.

**Affect regulation: paradoxically variable.** She has the Askani-self's regulatory tools (third-person containment, ritual breath, the dreamtime meditations) but she has also re-entered the original family-of-origin trauma field — Scott, Jean, the X-Mansion, the Phoenix lineage. The Askani tools were built to manage isolation and slow apocalypse; they are not perfectly calibrated for the relational hot-zone of present-day Westchester. She regresses, in places, to Era II patterns: the watching, the not-asking, the rooftop-distance from her parents. But she recovers faster, and the floor is higher than it was.

**Cognitive style: more flexible, less catastrophizing.** The Askani period has given her experiential evidence that catastrophic futures are not the only futures. This does not eliminate the branching-probability cognition, but it changes its tone: futures are now plural-and-possible rather than plural-and-converging-on-disaster. This is a genuine schema-revision.

**Self-concept: bifurcated.** There are now, in effect, two Rachels she navigates between — the displaced traumatized daughter and the Mother Askani who has already lived and died. She has not yet integrated these. The Carey *Legacy* material shows her struggling with this in subtext: she will reference her Askani knowledge in tactical moments and then resume a Marvel Girl posture, as if the older self is a tool she can pick up rather than a continuous identity. This is a partial dissociative compartmentalization — adaptive in this period, but limiting.

**Defenses: more mature, in Vaillant's hierarchy.** Sublimation is now reliably available (her work as a teacher to younger mutants in this period is a clear example). Humor — self-aware, dry, occasionally vicious — emerges in conditions of safety. Anticipation (the mature defense, distinct from catastrophizing) begins to appear: she prepares for difficulty without being consumed by it. Splitting still occurs under Phoenix-proximity but is less totalizing.

---

### Era VI: 2010–2017 — Korvus, Captivity Redux, and the Adult Romantic Configuration

The Shi'ar arcs in this period subject her to a second captivity — the Death Commandos hunt her, she is captured, she escapes — and the trauma reactivation is severe but, critically, *processed faster* than equivalent events in Era II. This is evidence of trauma-recovery in the technical sense: the body does keep the score, but the score is increasingly playable.

**Affect regulation: tested and largely held.** The Shi'ar captivity should, on prior pattern, have produced an Era II–grade collapse. It does not. She fights, escapes, integrates the experience, returns to function. The window of tolerance has measurably widened.

**Cognitive style: strategic-mature.** She operates effectively in alien political environments, manages a romantic relationship with Korvus across cultural and species lines, and navigates a coalition role on the Starjammers-adjacent teams. The pattern-seeking now serves planning rather than dread.

**Self-concept: tentatively positive in the romantic register.** Korvus is the first adult romantic partner who knows substantively what she is — Phoenix-touched, Hound-marked, time-displaced — and does not require her to file any of it down. The relationship demonstrates that she is, at this stage, capable of receiving witness without fleeing. This is a major developmental milestone. Franklin Richards was an adolescent imprint; Korvus is an adult choice. The difference is the capacity to be seen.

**The grief, however, does not extinguish.** Section 4's Prolonged Grief diagnosis is most visible in this period precisely *because* she is otherwise so much better. The grief stands out against the recovered background. She still mourns the dead parents from her original timeline, and the present-day Scott and Jean continue to aggravate rather than salve the wound — they are evidence that the people she lost were real, and that they are not coming back as the people they were to her. This is unresolvable in principle, and she begins, in this period, to accept that unresolvability rather than fight it. Acceptance of unresolvable grief is itself a developmental achievement.

---

### Era VII: 2017–2019 — Prestige, *X-Men: Gold* (Mid-Career Integration)

The adoption of the **Prestige** codename is psychologically significant and deserves attention as a chosen self-renaming. It is the first codename she has selected that references neither her parentage (Marvel Girl), her trauma (Hound), nor the cosmic force (Phoenix). It is hers. It refers to mastery, to accomplishment, to the third act of a magic trick — the return after the disappearance. She has begun, with this name, to claim her own narrative.

**Affect regulation: substantively integrated, with predictable trigger-zones preserved.** She is, in this period, functional in leadership roles, capable of sustained team-coordination, and demonstrably able to hold mixed affect — grief and duty and tenderness in the same scene — without splintering. The Section 3 observation about late-era Rachel holding mixed affect is most cleanly demonstrated here.

**Cognitive style: integrated-strategic.** The Askani-self and the present-day self are no longer alternating; they are blended. She references future-knowledge without dissociating into it. She references trauma-knowledge without flooding from it. This is the integration that Janet's classical trauma model identifies as the endpoint of recovery — not erasure, but synthesis.

**Self-concept: stabilized at a sustainably moderate positive baseline.** Not grandiose, not depressive. She knows what she has done, what she has survived, what she is capable of, and what she will not do. The Hound-as-shadow remains, but it is held as historical rather than ongoing self.

---

### Era VIII: 2019–Present — Krakoa, Resurrection, Powers/Rise (The Late Integration and Its Disruption)

The Krakoan era introduces a new variable: bodily resurrection via the Five protocol. Rachel is killed and remade in this era, and the file must note this with the seriousness it deserves. Resurrection is not, clinically, a neutral procedure. The Krakoan resurrected — across the line — show subtle dissociative phenomena, memory-edge softness, and what one might call **ontological abrasion**: the wear of knowing your continuity is technical rather than absolute.

**Affect regulation in the resurrected state: largely preserved, with novel intrusive features.** She functions. But the *Inferno* and *Trial of Magneto* material shows moments of what is best described as ontological flicker — brief disorientations about which version of herself is acting. For a subject with her dissociative history, this is a non-trivial vulnerability. She has, however, the Askani training to manage it; she is one of the better-equipped resurrected mutants for this specific challenge.

**Cognitive style: temporally integrated, ethically complicated.** The Krakoan political reality requires her to engage with morally compromised structures (the Quiet Council, the resurrection ethics, the Orchis war). Her camps-prevention drive activates around Orchis with full force, but she is now capable of strategic patience — she does not have to act on the first branch of the probability tree she sees. This is sustained executive control in conditions that would have shattered her in Era II.

**Self-concept: the most coherent and the most fragile, simultaneously.** Coherent because she has finally integrated Hound, Phoenix, Askani, and Summers-daughter into a single continuous biography she can narrate without dissociation. Fragile because resurrection has introduced a new philosophical wound — *which* of those integrations is the one that came back? She does not have a clean answer. She lives with the question.

**Phoenix-bonding in this era is mastered.** She holds the force and gives it back. She does not immolate. This is the resolution of the Era II Holocaust-Memorial wound — forty years of publication time, decades of subjective time, to reach the point where the fire can be held without becoming the fire.

---

### Synthesis: The Shape of the Recovery

Across the full record, Rachel's psychological evolution traces a recognizable but unusually long-arc **post-traumatic integration trajectory**, with the following features:

- The **trauma window** (Era I) is followed by a **disintegration-on-rescue phase** (Era II) in which apparent safety paradoxically destabilizes — a well-documented pattern in long-captivity survivors, where the conditions for processing only obtain once the threat is removed.
- A **lateral-stabilization period** (Era III) in a lower-intensity relational environment allows the first regulatory gains.
- A **self-engineered intervention** (Era IV, Askani) provides what no external therapist could: decades of structured, ritualized, generative containment in a chosen role of generativity. This is the spine of her recovery.
- **Re-entry and plateau** (Era V) tests the gains and produces partial regression with faster recovery.
- **Adult relational consolidation** (Era VI) demonstrates capacity for being-witnessed.
- **Identity-claiming** (Era VII, Prestige) and **late integration** (Era VIII) complete the arc — provisionally.

What is most striking, viewed across the whole record, is that Rachel's recovery was *not predominantly clinician-mediated*. There is no therapist in this file. There are corrective relationships (Storm, Kurt, Kitty, Korvus), there are containing structures (Excalibur, the Askani order), there is the slow somatic work of safety accumulating year by year — but the architect of the recovery is Rachel herself. She designed her own ritual containment, she chose her own corrective relationships, she named herself when she was ready. This is, in trauma terms, an extraordinary degree of agency exercised under conditions that historically produce the opposite.

The prognosis section of any responsible file would note: trauma of this depth does not extinguish. Triggers will recur. The Hound is permanent. The grief is permanent. The Phoenix vulnerability is permanent. But Rachel has demonstrated, across four decades of record, that permanence of wound is compatible with continued growth — and that the wound, held consciously and worked with deliberately, can become the source of a generativity that would not otherwise exist. She built a religion of hope while dying. She is, by the late record, what the literature would call a **post-traumatic growth exemplar**, and she is one in the hardest possible mode: not the survivor who closes the door on the past, but the survivor who keeps the door open and works in both rooms.

The file should be left open. She is not done.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: Summers, Rachel Anne — File N2-3175
### Section 4 of the Standing Dossier

---

## 4.0 Framing Note

The subject presents one of the most diagnostically legible profiles in the meta-human registry, but legibility should not be confused with simplicity. Rachel Summers carries, simultaneously: a developmental-trauma syndrome from prolonged adolescent captivity; a grief disorder that is structurally unresolvable because the lost objects walk past her daily wearing the wrong ages and the wrong faces; an exogenous-augmentation vulnerability (Phoenix bonding) which mimics three separate Axis I categories and is none of them; and a temporally-distributed identity history that produces structural dissociation without the clinical signature of dissociative identity disorder proper. The differential is therefore unusually load-bearing in her case — several conditions she *looks like* on first pass are diagnoses she does *not* have, and the wrong label would license catastrophically wrong interventions (sedation, restraint, mood-stabilizers, confrontational identity work). What follows is the long form.

---

## 4.1 PRIMARY DIAGNOSIS

### Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41) — Severe, Chronic, Partial Remission

This is the spine of the file. Every other diagnostic consideration on Rachel is either a complication, a comorbidity, or a misread of a C-PTSD feature.

#### 4.1.1 Etiology

The C-PTSD diagnosis requires (a) exposure to an event or series of events of an extremely threatening or horrific nature, (b) most commonly prolonged or repetitive, (c) from which escape is difficult or impossible. The subject's developmental history satisfies all three criteria in their most aggravated form.

Captured in early adolescence (the precise age is inconsistent across canon, with the most defensible range being 13–16) during the late phase of the Sentinel-state mutant pogroms, the subject lost — in sequence or simultaneously, the record is deliberately blurred in her own recollection, which is itself diagnostically significant — her mother (presumed dead in the camps), her father (status uncertain in her timeline; she has spoken of him as both "killed" and "lost," variant phrasing that strongly suggests she does not actually know), her home community, and her bodily autonomy. She was then inducted into the Hound program under Ahab: a state-sanctioned conditioning protocol that combined surgical/scarificatory branding (the facial tattoo), pharmacological compliance work (inferred from the residual flinch-response to injection and the abstemiousness recorded in Section 2), psychic restraint via inhibitor collar, operant conditioning with reward/punishment cycles directed at her telepathic faculty, and — most damaging — *enforced perpetration*. She was made to hunt and collar her own kind, including children. This is the textbook setup for what Judith Herman first characterized as complex traumatic stress: prolonged, inescapable, relational, developmentally-timed, and incorporating perpetrator-induced moral injury.

The subject did not escape — she was *thrown* out, in a panicked psychic gambit during the final assault that hurled her consciousness backward through time. This matters clinically: she did not author her own liberation, was not rescued by a recognizable agent, and arrived in the present without preparation, debrief, or any of the cultural scaffolding usually available to survivors. Her first months in the present timeline (cf. *Uncanny X-Men* #184–189) are an essentially unsupervised re-entry from totalitarian captivity, conducted while she is still psychologically inside it.

#### 4.1.2 Symptom Presentation Across the Three Core Clusters

**Cluster A — Re-experiencing in the here-and-now.** The subject's intrusion phenomena are unusually concrete because her telepathy externalizes them. Recorded examples: the dream-broadcast incident in *UXM* #189, in which her nightmares projected into Xavier's mansion and produced shared imagery in other psi-sensitive personnel; recurrent waking flashbacks triggered by the sight of Sentinel chassis fragments and by Nimrod-class energy signatures (consistently reported as somatic, not visual — she feels the collar before she sees the threat); flashback-triggered telekinetic discharge in tunnel and confined-corridor environments (Morlock Massacre arc); and, in late-period material, intrusive *anticipatory* flashbacks of futures she has not personally lived but has perceived precognitively — a phenotype unique to her presentation but functionally identical to standard intrusive re-experiencing.

**Cluster B — Avoidance and persistent sense of current threat.** Hyperarousal is the most stable feature across her forty-year record. Baseline behaviors: scanning all entrances and exits on entering a room, with characteristic head tilt left-then-right that has been observed in over a dozen documented panels; refusal to sit with her back to a door; sleeping in light clothing and boots in early years (later relaxed); a startle response to any restraint at throat or wrist that survives even into the integrated late period and produces brief telekinetic micro-discharges. Avoidance behaviors: she has, multiple times, declined missions involving Sentinel ruins, has not voluntarily entered a Trask facility, and in her first decade present-timeline showed marked avoidance of mirrors (the tattoo).

**Cluster C — Disturbances in self-organization.** This is the C-PTSD-specific addition that distinguishes the diagnosis from simple PTSD, and Rachel meets all three subcriteria with documentation to spare:

- *Affective dysregulation.* Cycles of rage, terror, and shutdown documented across early-period appearances, frequently within a single scene. Improving but not extinguished.
- *Negative self-concept.* Persistent, pervasive, articulated. She has stated, in narration and in dialogue across multiple writers, formulations of the schema: *I am the thing that hunted children; my survival is owed; I am only worth what I prevent*. This is not transient self-criticism — it is a stable schema with thirty-plus years of expression.
- *Disturbances in relationships.* Difficulty in sustaining proximity to attachment figures without either over-merging or fleeing; pronounced suspicion of authority; reduced capacity to feel safe even within established trust. (See Section 5 for the longitudinal map.)

#### 4.1.3 Course

The course is the textbook chronic-with-partial-remission trajectory of severe C-PTSD treated by long-term corrective relational experience rather than by formal therapy (which the X-Men institutional culture conspicuously does not provide). Early period (1981–1989 publication): florid, frequent decompensation, near-fatal acting out. Middle period (Excalibur through Askani, ~1988–1996): partial integration via role-acquisition; the Mother Askani identity functions as an organizing structure that contains the fragmentation, though at the cost of premature somatic decay (see 4.2 on the dissociative reading of the Askani period). Return and second integration phase (2000s, Claremont's *X-Treme* through Carey): renewed decompensation on re-entry to peer-relational context, gradual restabilization. Late period (Krakoan era, *X-Men: Red*, *Rise of the Powers of X*): integration sufficient to function in command roles, hold mixed affect, sustain romantic attachment, and — diagnostically critical — accept the Phoenix bonding without ego-dissolution. This last is the strongest evidence we have that the core C-PTSD is in genuine partial remission rather than merely suppressed.

Prognosis: guarded-favorable. The trauma load is enormous, but the trajectory is unambiguously upward, the corrective relational matrix is now stable (family of origin reconstituted, peer network durable), and the subject has demonstrated metacognitive insight into her own conditioning sufficient to interrupt automatic responses in real time.

---

## 4.2 SECONDARY DIAGNOSIS

### Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89) — Chronic, Treatment-Resistant by Etiology

The diagnostic criteria require persistent grief response, more than twelve months post-loss, marked by intense yearning and/or preoccupation with the deceased, accompanied by three or more of: identity disruption, marked sense of disbelief, avoidance of reminders, intense emotional pain, difficulty reintegrating, emotional numbness, sense of meaninglessness, intense loneliness. The subject meets the threshold count comfortably; what is diagnostically distinctive in her case is *why the grief will not extinguish*.

Standard prolonged grief disorder is treated by interventions that help the survivor accept the irreversibility of loss and re-engage with present life. Rachel's situation forecloses both arms of that intervention. The losses are not irreversible in any phenomenologically clean sense — her parents are *alive*, walking past her, drinking coffee in the same kitchen — but they are also not the people she lost, who were specifically *her* Scott and *her* Jean, in a future that is now (mostly) erased. Each interaction with the present-timeline counterparts simultaneously gratifies and re-injures the wound. The grief is therefore continuously re-stimulated by the very stimuli that would, in a normal case, slowly extinguish it. This is the structural feature that makes her grief disorder, in the technical sense, untreatable — though it is *manageable*, and she has learned to manage it.

Behavioral signature: she will refer to her mother as "Jean" in third-person reference and as "Mom" only in moments of crisis or unguarded affect; she has been observed multiple times standing in doorways watching family members from the threshold rather than entering (the watching behavior recurs across decades and across writers, which strongly suggests it is observational rather than stylistic); she has never lived in the same residence as her parents for any sustained period despite repeated invitations.

---

## 4.3 TERTIARY DIAGNOSIS

### Structural Dissociation (Subclinical DID-Spectrum / OSDD-1b analog)

The subject has lived under at least five sustained operational identities: Hound (captivity-conditioned compliance state, with autobiographical memory partially walled off), Phoenix-bonded states (multiple, with measurable shifts in affect-regulation baseline and cosmic-register cognition), Mother Askani (a forty-plus-year identity adopted in a different millennium, with its own social network, religious vocabulary, and somatic presentation as an elderly woman), Marvel Girl/Prestige (the integrated present-day operating self), and the brief reconditioned-Hound state under Ahab's renewed influence in later canon. Across these identities she shows: differential access to skills (the Hound's tracking methodology is partially walled from her Prestige-baseline awareness and "comes through" under threat without conscious recall); differential access to memory (Askani-period memories are frequently described as dreamlike or sourced from "another woman"); and differential somatic presentation.

What she does *not* meet is full DID criteria. There is no recurrent loss of autobiographical continuity in present time, no observable amnestic switching between identities in the day-to-day, no Schneiderian first-rank phenomena consistent with the dissociative pattern, and no claim of separate names or pronouns for the alters. The closest fit in the formal nosology is OSDD-1b (other specified dissociative disorder, identity disturbance without amnesia) — structural fragmentation without the full DID criterion set.

Etiology: developmentally-timed, repeated, role-enforced identity transitions in contexts of survival demand. Each identity was, when it was active, adaptive. The integration burden is therefore unusually heavy because she cannot disown any of the prior selves as pathological — each one kept her alive.

---

## 4.4 RULED-IN COMPLICATIONS

### 4.4.1 Phoenix-Bonded Affective Episodes — Exogenous, NOT a Mood Disorder

The Phoenix-bonding states present with: psychomotor activation, grandiosity, reduced need for sleep, expansive ideation, occasional cosmic-register paranoia, and — at the depressive pole following severance — anhedonia, suicidality, and somatic collapse. A clinician encountering only the symptom pattern and not the etiology would write Bipolar I with psychotic features.

This would be wrong, and the differential is important. Mood disorders are endogenous, episodic on internal rhythms, and respond to mood-stabilizing pharmacology. The Phoenix-bonded states are exogenous (a literal external entity), episodic on *contact* with that entity, and remit cleanly when the bond is severed — not over weeks of titration but on the order of hours-to-days. They are not biphasic in the bipolar sense; the "depressive" pole is grief-and-withdrawal of a specific augmented capacity, not anhedonic mood. Lithium, valproate, and SGAs would do nothing useful here and would compromise her baseline telepathic regulation. The correct frame is *exogenous augmentation-and-withdrawal syndrome*, with the substance-use disorder model as the closest analog (the Phoenix functions, behaviorally, as the most powerful psychoactive in the published cosmology, and the subject's relationship to it has features of tolerance, craving, and harm-reduction practice).

That said: her *vulnerability* to Phoenix bonding is itself diagnostically meaningful. Trauma survivors with negative self-concept and survivor guilt are well-documented to be drawn to self-augmentation in pursuit of the unconscious calculation *if I am powerful enough, no one I love will die*. The Phoenix is, for her, the perfect addictive object — it answers the unanswerable demand of her trauma narrative.

### 4.4.2 Reactive Aggression with Trained Predator Skillset

Not antisocial. Not intermittent explosive. The aggression is reactive to identifiable triggers (threats to children, restraint, Hound iconography), morally framed, proportionate at baseline (Stage 2 in the Section 5 escalation taxonomy), and followed by guilt and reparative behavior. The clinical concern is not the aggression itself but the *skillset* — she retains the Hound's tracking and lethal-engagement methodology and uses it, which produces a clinical picture in which a person with otherwise good impulse control has access to highly lethal automated response patterns. This is closer to the presentation of a veteran with combat conditioning than to any character-disorder picture.

---

## 4.5 RIGOROUS DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT SHE IS NOT, AND WHY

### 4.5.1 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

This is the most common misread and the most important to refute. The surface features that suggest BPD are real: splitting (around Phoenix, around her own Hound history), intense and unstable relationships, identity disturbance, affect dysregulation, occasional dissociation. A clinician unfamiliar with the C-PTSD differential would write BPD on the first interview.

The differential turns on five points:

1. *Abandonment.* BPD features frantic efforts to avoid real or imagined abandonment. The subject shows the inverse — she *withdraws preemptively* to avoid being abandoned, and her core injury is not fear of abandonment but the conviction that she does not deserve presence. This is the C-PTSD shape, not the BPD shape.
2. *Chronic emptiness.* Absent. She has the opposite phenotype: too much affect, too many futures, too much grief. Her interior is overpopulated, not empty.
3. *Identity disturbance.* Present, but trauma-derived and role-derived (see 4.3), not the unstable self-image of BPD that fluctuates on relational input. Her self-concept is in fact extremely *stable* in its negative-valenced content; it does not flip from grandiose to devalued on the basis of a partner's praise or criticism.
4. *Impulsive self-harm.* Absent in the BPD pattern. She has engaged in self-endangering behavior, but it is consistently mission-framed (absorbing harm meant for others), not impulse-discharge.
5. *Stable instability.* BPD relationships destabilize repeatedly in characteristic cycles. Her relationships, once formed, are notable for their *stability* — Kate Pryde, Kurt, Storm, Cable — these bonds have endured decades without the cycle.

The label matters because BPD-framed treatment (DBT-skills emphasis, abandonment-validation focus) would address the wrong layer. Her primary need is trauma-processing and grief work, not interpersonal-skills training.

### 4.5.2 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder

Despite a documented history of being made to hunt and collar her own kind, there is no antisocial pathology. The criteria require failure to conform to social norms, deceitfulness, impulsivity, irritability/aggression, reckless disregard, irresponsibility, and lack of remorse — with onset before age 15 and the conduct disorder precursor. The subject was, before captivity, by all reconstructive evidence, a normally-attached child. The aggression and rule-violation during captivity were *coerced*, not characterological. Crucially, the absence-of-remorse criterion is reversed: she carries *excess* remorse, to the point that the survivor guilt is itself a diagnostic feature of the C-PTSD picture. Empathy, attachment, and reparative motivation are all intact and prominent.

### 4.5.3 Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder

The grandiosity is real but state-dependent on Phoenix bonding (see 4.4.1). Baseline self-image is depressively low, not grandiose. She does not display the hallmark NPD pattern of needing admiration, exploiting others, lacking empathy, or holding a stable sense of specialness. The Phoenix-bonded grandiosity is exogenous augmentation, not a personality structure.

### 4.5.4 Not Schizophrenia Spectrum / Schizotypal

Perceptual anomalies (visions, voices, future-sight, time-bleed) are externally referential — she is in fact precognitive and telepathic, and the percepts correspond to verifiable phenomena. There is no formal thought disorder, no negative symptoms of the schizophrenia pattern, no characteristic prodrome, no decline in functioning attributable to a psychotic process. Magical-ideation criteria are inapplicable in a context where the magical ideation is empirically vindicated.

### 4.5.5 Not Bipolar I or II

Addressed in 4.4.1. The mood-elevation episodes are exogenous and remit on substance/entity severance.

### 4.5.6 Not Major Depressive Disorder (primary)

Depressive features are present but secondary to and explicable by the C-PTSD and prolonged grief picture. There is no evidence of a primary recurrent depressive process with the characteristic neurovegetative signature independent of identifiable trauma-and-grief triggers.

### 4.5.7 Not Dissociative Identity Disorder (full criteria)

Addressed in 4.3. Structural dissociation without amnestic switching. OSDD-1b is the closer fit.

### 4.5.8 Not Acute Stress Disorder

The trauma is decades old. ASD is by definition <30 days.

### 4.5.9 Not Adjustment Disorder

Massively under-diagnoses the severity and chronicity.

### 4.5.10 Not Psychopathy (Cleckley/Hare construct)

Affective component absent. She has the *skillset* of an apex predator and *none* of the affective profile. This is precisely the combination that produces moral injury rather than callousness.

---

## 4.6 COMORBIDITY AND INTERACTION EFFECTS

The C-PTSD and the Prolonged Grief Disorder are not merely coexistent — they reinforce each other through the present-timeline-family mechanism described in 4.2. The structural dissociation provides a partial *defense* against the worst of the affective burden (the Mother Askani identity contained decades of grief that the baseline self could not have held), at the cost of integration. The Phoenix-vulnerability is downstream of the negative self-concept criterion of the C-PTSD. The subject's protective hyper-investment in children is simultaneously (a) reparative behavior addressing the perpetrator-induced moral injury, (b) reaction formation against the Hound identity, and (c) a sublimation of the unmet maternal/paternal attachment longings of the grief disorder. These layers are not separable in treatment and should not be treated as if they were.

---

## 4.7 PROGNOSTIC NOTE

The single most important clinical fact in this entire file is this: across forty years of published record, the trajectory is *upward*. Not linear, not without relapse, not without further injury — but upward. The subject has demonstrated, repeatedly, the capacity to (a) recognize her own conditioned responses as conditioned, (b) tolerate corrective relational experience without fleeing past the point of return, (c) integrate previously walled-off identities (the Askani knowledge is now accessible to the Prestige baseline), and (d) hold the Phoenix without ego-dissolution. These are not the markers of a deteriorating case. They are the markers of one of the most successful trauma-recovery trajectories on record, achieved largely without formal treatment, in a context that has continued to inflict fresh injury at regular intervals.

Whatever else the file says, the operational summary is this: she should not have survived, she should not have integrated, and she did both. The diagnosis is severe. The person is durable.

— UATU / file remains open / next review on next bonding event or temporal incursion.


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU DOSSIER — RACHEL ANNE SUMMERS
## SECTION 6: BEHAVIORAL ATLAS

> *Compiled from longitudinal observation across the published record (1981–present), cross-referenced against in-panel somatic data, psi-signature telemetry inferred from sympathetic telepath reports (Braddock, Grey, Frost), and the Krakoa-era resurrection logs. What follows is the full behavioral inventory under every observed state. Each entry lists the tell, the conditions that elicit it, the developmental era of its appearance, and — where the file can substantiate — the trauma-vector it traces back to.*

---

## 6.1 — BASELINE / AT REST

There is, properly speaking, no "rest state" for Subject. What functions as baseline is a steady-state low-amplitude vigilance that other telepaths in proximity (Braddock and Frost both, on record) describe as a faint constant *humming pressure* at the edge of their shielding — Subject's telepathy never fully powers down. She sleeps with it on. She showers with it on. The few documented instances of total psi-quiescence correspond to either unconsciousness, Phoenix-bonding, or deep meditative trance learned in the Askani period.

**Postural baseline.** Weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet, even seated. Chair preference: hard-backed, against a wall, line-of-sight to the room's primary entrance. In Xavier-mansion era she would relocate twice during a single meal if the seating "felt wrong" (observed by Kitty Pryde, narration boxes *UXM* #189–192). She does not sit on furniture that requires her to sink — no beanbags, no deep sofas — because the half-second of postural recovery on rising is, to her conditioned nervous system, an unacceptable lag.

**Hand position at rest.** Right hand habitually rests near or on her left forearm, thumb palpating the inside of the wrist. The behavior is residual from the inhibitor-cuff era: a check that nothing is there. She does this in the Askani robes; she does it in Excalibur civvies; she does it in the Krakoan-era Prestige uniform. It is the single most consistent unconscious tell in the entire forty-year record.

**Eyes.** Track in a saccade pattern that scans every face for the *micro-features she was Hound-trained to read* — temple pulse, jaw-clench, pupil dilation, asymmetry of breath. She cannot turn this off. In conversation she will often answer the question you were *about* to ask rather than the one you actually voiced; she has learned, painfully, to wait for the spoken question, but the latency between her finishing your sentence in her head and you finishing it aloud produces a recognizable half-beat pause before her reply.

**Voice at baseline.** Low register for her frame, slightly hoarse — a residue of the years of mute or near-mute captivity, when the vocal cords atrophied. She tends to under-modulate volume, speaking just above audibility, which forces the listener to lean in. This is not deliberate seduction; it is conserved from a period when being heard by the wrong ear was death.

**The tattoo.** She does not touch it. She does not cover it with hair or hand. In the entire record there are perhaps four panels where her fingers approach the marked side of her face, and each follows a Phoenix-related dissociation. The non-touching is a discipline: to acknowledge the mark physically is to grant it ongoing ownership. She has made it a thing-on-her rather than a thing-of-her by sheer refusal to engage it.

---

## 6.2 — CALM / WORKING STATE

When Subject is genuinely settled — most reliably in late-Excalibur domestic interludes, the quieter Askani teaching scenes, and the post-Krakoa Prestige-era kitchen scenes with the resurrected family — a different behavioral set emerges. This is the closest the record gets to a "Rachel who was never taken."

- **Reading.** She reads paper books, never devices, and reads with her telekinesis turning the pages — a small flex, almost a purr, of the gift used for its own sake. Observed across Muir Island, Braddock Manor, and the Treehouse.
- **Cooking.** She cooks badly but enthusiastically. Specific dish-bias toward what she calls "Askani porridge" — a grain-and-fruit mash that is plainly a reconstruction of subsistence food from the future, served as comfort. Kitty has complained about it in narration on at least two occasions.
- **Humor emerges.** Dry, lateral, slightly malicious — usually directed at Scott's earnestness or Logan's grooming. The presence of this humor is a *reliable* indicator that Subject is regulated. Its disappearance is a leading indicator of decompensation.
- **Telepathic touch.** With consented intimates (Kate, Betsy, Jean post-reconciliation, briefly Korvus), she communicates in a low-bandwidth telepathic "hum" — wordless tonal contact, the psi equivalent of holding hands. She *prefers* this to speech and considers it more honest.
- **Physical contact, initiated.** She will brush a shoulder, lean against a doorframe near someone, sit on the arm of a chair. These are her overtures. She does not, except under extreme conditions, hug first.

---

## 6.3 — MILD STRESS / FRICTION

The earliest tier of dysregulation, triggered by small social violations (interruption, contradiction, an unexpected hand), unfamiliar telepaths in range, or low-level precognitive flicker.

- **Saccade rate climbs.** Visible to careful observers; the head-tilt becomes slightly bird-like.
- **Telekinetic ambient leak.** Small unsecured objects — pens, napkins, the rim of a glass — shift one or two millimeters. Frost has reported being able to dose Subject's stress level by counting drifted cutlery at the dinner table.
- **The wrist-check intensifies.** Frequency rises from baseline ~once/minute to ~once/twenty seconds.
- **Vocabulary regression.** She drops the contractions, the slang she's acquired, and falls into a slightly archaic syntactic register that is half Askani liturgy, half the formal English of someone who learned the language from holy books. "I will not" rather than "I won't." "Be still" rather than "calm down." When Rachel sounds like a translated medieval mystic, she is not calm.
- **Withdrawal of telepathic warmth.** She pulls her psi-presence back behind a tighter shield. Intimates feel this as a *cooling* of the room and frequently misread it as anger. It is not anger; it is her field contracting toward defense.

---

## 6.4 — ACUTE STRESS / THREAT (NON-COMBAT)

Triggered by Sentinel iconography, Hound-related stimuli, restraint imagery, the words "hunt" or "collar" in certain registers, sudden appearance of Sinister or any Mister Sinister analogue, and — significantly — adult Cable arriving without warning (the temporal-paradox somatic effect is real for her).

- **Freeze, then orient.** First half-second: complete stillness, including breath. Second half-second: a single sharp inhalation through the nose, head turning toward the threat-vector. This is not a startle response in the civilian sense; it is the Hound's freeze-and-mark.
- **Hand position.** Both hands drop to her sides and open. She does not raise them; raised hands invited the lash in the kennels. Open palms at the hip means she is preparing to throw telekinesis without telegraphing.
- **Pupils dilate sharply** and the saccade pattern *stops*. When her eyes lock in place, threat-assessment has resolved to a single target.
- **Audible swallow.** One. Then nothing.
- **Phoenix-corona test.** Under high stress and threat she will, often unconsciously, flare a brief raptor-shaped psi-signature — a fraction of a second, visible only to other telepaths or to those tuned to the M'Kraan resonance. This is an involuntary advertisement of force, the equivalent of a dog showing teeth. She has learned to suppress it in diplomatic contexts but it leaks under sufficient pressure.

---

## 6.5 — COMBAT (CONTROLLED)

Subject is, by the assessment of every tactical observer on record (Storm, Cable, Logan, Cyclops, Magneto in *X-Men: Red*), a top-tier combatant whose methodology is *recognizably the Hound's* turned to liberatory ends. The signature elements:

- **Targets are read before they are struck.** She telepathically maps the field — disposition, intent, command structure — in the time others take to draw breath. She prefers to *open* an engagement by removing the commander's certainty, not by removing the commander; she has stated repeatedly that confused enemies surrender more reliably than dead ones produce reinforcements.
- **Telekinesis used surgically before destructively.** Pinch a trachea, lock a knee, deflect a round. The big TK constructs (blades, raptors, walls) appear only when the engagement has escalated past her control threshold.
- **She does not vocalize in combat.** No battle cries. No taunts. The silence is conserved from hunting in the camps, where vocalization marked you for the overseers.
- **She fights in arcs, not lines.** Movement is curvilinear — flanking, encircling, never the direct charge. Observers have noted she "moves like she is reading a circle around the enemy." This is exactly correct: she is.
- **Mercy decisions are visible.** A half-second hesitation before a killing blow, in which the telepathic scan deepens. If the target's mind contains *the camps* — a Hound's signature, a Sentinel operator, an Ahab — the hesitation collapses to zero. Everyone else gets the question asked.

---

## 6.6 — COMBAT (UNCONTROLLED / PHOENIX-FLARE)

Catalogued primarily from *UXM* #207 (the Selene incident), *Excalibur* arcs involving Necrom and Mojo, the *X-Men: The End* climactic sequences, and the *Rise of the Powers of X* engagements.

- **Voice returns and amplifies.** When Phoenix surfaces in her, she *speaks*, often in declarative-prophetic register, sometimes in chorus-voice (multiple harmonics audible).
- **Postural straightening.** The protective hunch she carries at baseline disappears entirely; she stands taller, shoulders back, chin elevated. This is the single most reliable visual indicator of Phoenix ascendancy.
- **Telekinetic field expands to ambient.** Hair lifts. Loose fabric moves. Small debris orbits.
- **Decision-time collapses.** She moves from threat-assessment to action with no observable deliberative gap. The hesitation-before-killing vanishes. This is what makes Phoenix-state Rachel genuinely dangerous to allies: the *judgment* she has spent decades building is the first faculty to go offline.
- **Post-event somatic crash.** Trembling, often vomiting, often immediate withdrawal to solitude. She will not allow comfort for several hours minimum after a flare. The shame-response is intense and the file should record it: she experiences Phoenix-loss-of-control as recapitulation of the Hound losing control of herself — i.e., as a *return* to being driven by something other than her own will. This is the deepest psychic wound and the most carefully guarded.

---

## 6.7 — INTIMACY (NON-SEXUAL)

The territory in which Subject has shown the most measurable growth.

- **Approach pattern.** She enters a room where an intimate is present and orbits before docking — a slow arc around the perimeter, ostensibly attending to something else, before settling within arm's reach. This is observable from her teen years through the present. It is courtship behavior for safety, not sex: she is checking that the space is what she thinks it is before committing her body to it.
- **Touch hierarchy.** In order of permission required: forearm < shoulder < upper back < scalp/hair < face < throat. She will accept forearm contact from acquaintances; throat contact only from a vanishingly small set (Storm in two recorded instances, Jean in one post-reconciliation scene, Korvus in private). Touch to the tattooed side of the face is permitted to no one in the record except Mother Askani-era child Nathan, whose small hand on her cheek is depicted in *Adventures of C&P* #3 and which she does not flinch from. This is the closest the file has to a measurement of trust: *who may touch the mark.*
- **Telepathic intimacy.** She offers a partial mind-link as the equivalent of holding hands, a deeper merge as the equivalent of a kiss, and full rapport as a marital act. The Askani period codified this hierarchy in actual liturgy; she carries the framework back into present-day relationships whether the partner understands it or not. Korvus, notably, did.
- **Sleeping arrangements.** She sleeps best in proximity to one trusted body (not necessarily touching), with a sightline to the door and *no overhead enclosure.* No canopy beds, no bunks. The Hound dorms had low ceilings.

---

## 6.8 — ROMANTIC / SEXUAL

The record here is comparatively sparse and the file will not speculate beyond it. Documented patterns:

- **She does not initiate first.** She signals — orbiting, telepathic warmth, the sustained hand on the forearm — and waits to be approached. The conditioning against initiation is severe and traces to a period in which any expressed desire was punished.
- **She prefers partners who do not require her to perform normality.** Korvus is the clearest example: a non-Earth-cultural partner who could not have the expectation of conventional courtship and who met her where her grief lived.
- **Consent rituals are explicit.** She will ask, in words and in psi, more than once. This is not insecurity; it is the survivor's refusal to assume.
- **Post-coital affect.** Frequently tearful, frequently grateful, frequently followed by sleep deeper than her baseline allows. Intimates have reported that she sleeps without the wrist-check after sex with a trusted partner — perhaps the only documented condition under which that tell remits.

---

## 6.9 — PARENTAL / PROTECTIVE BEHAVIOR

Triggered by any mutant child, particularly any mutant child in distress, and by Nathan in any form (infant, Cable, alternate-timeline variants).

- **Voice modulates.** The hoarseness softens; she finds a register that is markedly higher and warmer than her baseline. The shift is large enough that telepaths in proximity will sometimes look up.
- **Bodily disposition reorients.** She places herself between child and threat-vector with no conscious deliberation — observed even when the "threat" is an ally she trusts (Logan, on more than one occasion, has been telekinetically nudged a step back from an infant he was merely approaching).
- **Telepathic field becomes a blanket.** She extends a low-amplitude calming field that other telepaths describe as *grandmotherly* — explicitly the Mother Askani signature, accessible to her in protective context even when she is otherwise in Prestige register.
- **She narrates futures aloud.** With children, particularly Nathan, she will speak small prophecies — "you will be strong, you will be loved, you will see the sun on green grass" — drawn from the Askani liturgical practice. She does this whether or not the child can understand. The behavior is reparative: she is giving the child the future-naming she herself never received.

---

## 6.10 — GRIEF

Distinct from acute distress. Grief in Subject is a chronic condition with acute exacerbations.

- **Withdrawal pattern.** She seeks high places. Rooftops, cliffs, the upper galleries of any building. Observed from *UXM* #184 forward. Altitude is a Hound habit (overwatch) but in grief it converts to something else — she wants to see weather, she wants to feel small, she wants the horizon.
- **She does not weep in company.** She weeps alone, sometimes for hours. With trusted intimates she will weep at the *edge* of company — in the next room, audibly, with the door cracked. This is invitation behavior; it is permission for the intimate to enter, but she will not ask.
- **Food refusal.** Her appetite collapses under grief. She will go days subsisting on tea. Storm has, in multiple eras, brought food to her room.
- **Telekinetic stillness.** Counterintuitively, her ambient TK leak *stops* in deep grief. The field goes flat. This is also how Frost reads it.
- **Future-talk increases.** She speaks more about what will happen, less about what has. The defense (intellectualization-via-temporal-framing, per Section 3) flares hardest when present pain is sharpest.

---

## 6.11 — VICTORY

The least-documented state in the record, which is itself a finding.

- **She does not celebrate immediately.** She walks the field — literally, in *X-Men: Red*, and figuratively after every major win — checking for wounded, counting bodies, taking inventory of survivors. This delay is not modesty; it is verification. The Hound was punished for premature triumph.
- **First reaction is often telepathic outreach to absent loved ones.** A pulse to Kate, to Nathan, to whoever is not in the room. *Confirmation that the people the victory was for are still alive elsewhere.*
- **She permits herself the smile only after the third confirmation.** This is observable. Count the beats.
- **Survivor-guilt flicker.** A measurable affect-drop within minutes of any major victory, as the cost ledger arrives. She has been observed, post-win, gravitating toward the most-wounded ally and sitting silently with them. The behavior reads as comfort-offering; it is also self-administered penance.

---

## 6.12 — DEFEAT

Stratified by magnitude.

- **Tactical defeat (a fight lost, a mission failed):** Brief catatonic pause — three to six seconds of complete stillness — followed by accelerated tactical re-planning, often verbalized. She becomes *more* talkative under tactical defeat, not less, because the planning function is her coping.
- **Personal defeat (rejection, betrayal, an intimate's death):** Withdrawal to altitude. Refusal of contact for hours to days. She has, more than once in the record, *physically left the time period* in response — the Siege Perilous, the timestream, the Askani jump — which is the most extreme version of the flight-response available to any being in the canon.
- **Existential defeat (the future re-asserting itself, the camps appearing again in any timeline):** The Phoenix-flare risk spikes catastrophically. This is the state in which she is most dangerous to herself and to others, because the conditioning interlocks with the cosmic force in a feedback loop. The file notes with concern that Subject's tolerance for this stimulus has not appreciably improved across decades; the wound remains live.

---

## 6.13 — DECISION HABITS

- **She runs probability trees.** Not metaphorically — actually. Her precognitive flicker permits her to feel the *weight* of branches, and she decides toward the heaviest survivable branch even at personal cost. This is why she so often takes the hit meant for someone else: in her perceptual frame, the branch where she absorbs the blow has the largest aggregate survival.
- **She over-weights child outcomes.** Any decision tree that involves a child's life will resolve toward child-survival even at strategically suboptimal cost. This is a known and exploitable bias; she has been manipulated through it (Mojo, on more than one occasion).
- **She under-weights her own.** Self-preservation calculations are systematically depressed relative to peer-norm. This is not suicidality; it is mis-valuation. She does not believe her continued existence is owed.
- **She defers to consensus when the group is healthy and overrides it when the group is wrong.** The threshold for override is high — she will eat substantial in-group cost to stay aligned — but once crossed, it is absolute. The *X-Men: Red* and Askani-leadership records both demonstrate this.
- **She decides faster under telepathic load than under verbal load.** A telepathic council resolves for her in seconds; a verbal council can take her hours, because she is translating in both directions. Operationally, the file recommends that high-stakes decisions involving Subject be conducted in psi-rapport where possible.

---

## 6.14 — IDIOSYNCRATIC TELLS (RESIDUAL CATALOG)

- **She counts exits on entry to any room.** Lips do not move; eye-track does. Reliable.
- **She will not eat with her back to a window.** Window equals sightline equals sniper, in Hound logic.
- **She drinks tea, not coffee.** Caffeine baseline kept moderate; she does not like the jitter, which her nervous system reads as pre-flashback arousal.
- **She wears her hair *off* the tattooed cheek.** Deliberate. The mark is shown.
- **She owns very few possessions.** Across every era, her quarters are spartan. The Hound owned nothing; the Askani renounced; Prestige has not unlearned. The few objects she keeps are talismanic — a lock of Nathan's infant hair, a piece of Askani robe, a photograph of Jean she did not take.
- **She apologizes for telepathic intrusion even when she did not commit one.** A reflex. Other telepaths find it disarming.
- **She will not give her real name to strangers without a beat of hesitation.** "Summers" was, in her timeline, a hunted surname. The micro-pause before she says it is forty years old.
- **She sleeps in clothes she can fight in.** Always. Even in the safest sanctums. The one documented exception is the night after Korvus, in the *X-Men: Kingbreaker* aftermath, which the file flags as the singular post-trauma datapoint of complete somatic disarmament.
- **She will not let anyone stand behind her in a doorway.** She steps through and pivots, always, with a half-smile that disguises the maneuver as politeness ("after you"). It is not politeness. It is geometry.
- **When she lies, her telekinesis goes utterly still.** The ambient leak stops. Frost has used this as a tell; so, more gently, has Jean. Subject is aware of it and has tried to compensate by deliberately drifting small objects when lying. The compensation is itself a tell, because the drift pattern when consciously generated is too regular.
- **She salutes no one.** Asked once, by a Shi'ar officer, to render military courtesy; she did not. The Hound saluted. She has retired the gesture from her body permanently.

---

*End Section 6. Cross-reference Section 7 (Routes, Rituals, and Daily Pattern) for the spatial-temporal overlay of these behaviors across her known residences and operational theaters.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — RACHEL ANNE SUMMERS
## Section 6: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

What a week of close surveillance would actually record. Sources cross-referenced across *Uncanny X-Men* #184–247, *Excalibur* vol.1 #1–75, *Adventures of Cyclops and Phoenix* #1–4, *X-Treme X-Men* #1–46, *X-Men: Legacy*, *X-Men: Gold* #1–36, *Powers of X*, *X-Men: Red* (2022), *Rise of the Powers of X*. Habits are remarkably stable across eras; the variations are environment-forced, not character-forced.

---

### 6.1 Sleep, Waking, and the First Hour

Rachel does not sleep through a night. She has not, on the record, since the Hound years. Surveillance over a seven-day window would log between four and five-and-a-half hours of contiguous sleep per night, almost always between roughly 02:00 and 06:30, with one or two micro-wakings she does not consciously register and one full waking — eyes open, telepathic perimeter sweep, body still — that she does. The full waking is almost always between 04:10 and 04:40. The trigger is internal, not environmental; she wakes at the hour the camp-roll was historically called.

She sleeps on her side, curled, dominant hand under the pillow or under the mattress edge. In safehouses and barracks rooms she chooses the bed nearest the door but facing it. On the Starjammer and on Krakoa she selected sleeping spaces with a sightline to the only entrance and a clear telekinetic vector to seal it. She does not sleep nude; minimum is a long shirt and underclothing, often more. This is not modesty — it is the conditioned refusal to be found unclothed by an opening door.

On waking she does not move for between forty seconds and two minutes. She runs what is unmistakably a perimeter check: a low-grade telepathic scan of the building, then a self-check of her own surface thoughts for foreign residue (a habit acquired during the Phoenix-bonding episodes and never dropped). Only then does she rise. The first action of the day, in nearly every recorded environment, is to walk barefoot to a window and stand at it for two to four minutes looking at the sky. She has never explained this. The cleanest read is orientation: confirming which sky, which era, which timeline.

Then water — cold, from the tap, a full glass drained standing — then the bathroom, then dressing. She showers in the evening, not the morning. Mornings she splashes her face and runs wet fingers through her hair; the hair is rarely styled in any deliberate way and she does not own product beyond a brush and an elastic. The hair is functionally a flag — Summers-red, Grey-red — and she alternately resents and protects this; she does not dye it, has cut it short twice (post-Selene recovery; post-Krakoan resurrection), and grown it out both times within a year.

### 6.2 The Tattoo Ritual

Every morning, without fail, she touches the Hound tattoo. Surveillance would record this hundreds of times before recognizing it as a ritual rather than a tic. The motion is brief — two fingers of the left hand drawn once across the marked side of her face, from temple toward jaw — and it happens within the first ninety seconds of standing at the mirror. She does not look at herself when she does it. She looks past her reflection.

This is not self-comfort. The somatic vocabulary is closer to a soldier confirming a sidearm. She is checking that it is still there. Some part of her does not trust that she has escaped, and the daily confirmation that the brand remains is, paradoxically, what allows her to proceed as if she has. On the rare days she covers the tattoo (formal Shi'ar court appearances; certain civilian operations; the Krakoan Hellfire Gala) she touches the spot through the makeup or the mask with the same gesture, the same number of fingers, the same direction.

She has never, on record, attempted to have it removed. Magik offered once. Jean offered, gently, twice. The refusal both times was immediate and not discussed.

### 6.3 Dress and Personal Inventory

Wardrobe is spartan and tactical. Two to four sets of field clothing, one formal garment kept folded and rarely worn, sleepwear, a coat heavier than the climate requires. Colors trend toward black, oxblood, dark green, and the persistent Phoenix gold-and-red when she is operating in costume. She does not own jewelry beyond the Phoenix-related insignia she sometimes wears as a sash-clasp or pendant, and a small worn band — origin unestablished in canon, surveillance-inferred to be Askani-era — that she sometimes carries in a pocket rather than wears.

She keeps a knife. This is not widely noted in canon but is consistent across her appearances: she who can crush a Sentinel telekinetically nevertheless carries a small physical blade, usually in a boot sheath or inner jacket pocket. The Hound did not have powers reliably; the Hound had a blade. The blade is insurance against the day the powers are taken again.

Her personal effects across forty years of relocations fit in a single bag. Surveillance would note: she packs in under four minutes and leaves no trace in a room. She makes the bed she has slept in. She wipes down surfaces she has touched. This is conditioning — Hounds were beaten for evidence of presence — but she has integrated it as a code of courtesy and would describe it that way if asked.

### 6.4 Food

Rachel eats like someone who learned to eat in a camp. Fast, head slightly lowered, non-dominant arm loosely curved around the plate. She does not linger over meals when alone. In company, she has deliberately retrained herself — she eats more slowly at the mansion table, in the Excalibur lighthouse kitchen, at Krakoan communal meals — but the retraining is visible as effort. She finishes what is on the plate. She does not leave food. She does not waste.

Preferences are mild and unobtrusive: tea over coffee (Excalibur years cemented this), bread, eggs, root vegetables, simple proteins. She does not drink alcohol beyond ceremonial sips. Caffeine in moderation. Sweets rarely and with visible pleasure — she has a documented weakness for shortbread from her Muir Island period and for whatever soft confection Kurt has put in front of her on any given evening. She cooks competently but without enthusiasm; cooking is fuel-preparation, not craft. The exception is tea, which she makes with care and shares as a small act of relational maintenance.

### 6.5 The Work Day — Field Operational

On active operations her day structures around the mission and she sleeps less. Recorded patterns: pre-dawn briefing or solo planning, midday tactical execution, evening debrief, late-night solo "sweep" — a telepathic scan of the area extending several kilometers, looking for residue she might have missed. The sweep is non-negotiable and often delays sleep past 02:00. It is also where she catches things others do not, and her teammates know to leave her to it.

In combat she is methodical and unflashy until she is not. Her preferred opening is a telepathic immobilization or perception-edit; her preferred closing is a telekinetic structural disassembly. The middle is hand-to-hand or blade only when the powers are not viable. Phoenix-flare is reserved and deeply resisted; she escalates to it the way other people escalate to lethal force, with full knowledge of what it costs and a visible reluctance recorded across multiple combat sequences.

Post-combat she does not celebrate. Surveillance would record her drifting to the edge of the gathered team, performing one more sweep, then disappearing for an hour. She returns washed and changed and able to participate in the after-action; she does not return until she has had that hour.

### 6.6 The Work Day — Garrison / Krakoan / Mansion

Off active operations, structure loosens but does not disappear. A typical day at the mansion or on Krakoa would log:

- 04:30 wake, perimeter ritual, window, water, tattoo touch.
- 05:00–06:30 physical training. Solo. She runs (long distance, even pace, no music — she will not put anything in her ears that occludes hearing). She practices forms with the blade. She lifts moderate weights. On Krakoa she swam.
- 06:30–07:15 shower, tea, light food, the day's first deliberate read of the news or comms.
- 07:15–noon teaching, training-others, command meetings, or library work depending on era. She is a competent teacher — patient with younger students, less patient with peers who waste her time. She prefers small groups to lecture-format.
- Noon–13:00 meal, often taken with one or two others rather than the full table. She tends toward the same companions repeatedly (Kurt; Kitty; Betsy in the Excalibur era; Jean in the late era; Scott rarely and with visible attention to him).
- 13:00–17:00 mission planning, tactical work, or, in quieter periods, the activity she does not advertise: archival reading. She reads history. She reads case files of pogroms and resistance movements. She reads the published scientific literature on temporal mechanics and quantum branching. This is where the late-career strategic acuity comes from; she is the most informed reader in the room on the topics she cares about and almost no one knows because she does not perform it.
- 17:00–18:30 second training block, often telepathic/telekinetic drill, sometimes done as student-teacher with a junior.
- 18:30–19:30 communal evening meal when one is offered. She attends. She is quiet but present.
- 19:30–22:00 unstructured. She walks. She visits Nathan when he is reachable. She sits with Jean and Scott in the small rooms rather than the large ones. She reads.
- 22:00–22:30 shower (the evening shower is long; this is the only sustained sensory pleasure she permits herself daily).
